  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8f8e9682-c5bc-4737-ab48-a59d8617cc1f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer17020897539872319530">I just finished and I have a lot going through my head, so bare with me as I try to work it out into words. <br/><br/>Strange Angels is one of my favorite series. I love all three main characters, Dru, Graves and even Christophe. I love the dark and dirty writing and this last book of the series was excellent. There are certainly things that I will be complaining about in a bit, but as a whole I was pleased with the way the plot was finished. <br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ My main and pretty much only complaint I have i</span></span>
  <span id="freeText17020897539872319530" style="display:none">I just finished and I have a lot going through my head, so bare with me as I try to work it out into words. <br /><br />Strange Angels is one of my favorite series. I love all three main characters, Dru, Graves and even Christophe. I love the dark and dirty writing and this last book of the series was excellent. There are certainly things that I will be complaining about in a bit, but as a whole I was pleased with the way the plot was finished. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ My main and pretty much only complaint I have is the ending. It wasn't bad, it was actually like a breaath of fresh air after spending the last 4 3/4 books holding your breath. There are two main concerns in the story, one being the love triangle and the second being Sergej. Both of thse plot lines are satisfied at the end, which I was extremely happy about. I really dislike open ended books!!! Which brings me back to my main complaint...the love triangle. The ending was left open, but yet it wasn't. Let me explain. <br />Dru knows who she loves, but Graves has to leave to get good headspace after being broken, but leaves with a promise to come back. O.k., I understand that, but he was leaving without telling Dru, which was a TOTAL DICK MOVE!!! Christophe is left at the Schola with Dru and Dru gently tells him she's not interested...in anyone...right now... While she is blushing and stumbling as usual around Christophe. Talk about crossing wires! Sooooooooooooo I am assuming Graves is coming back to claim her. It's never said, but that's what my heart is telling me. There is even an epilogue, but no mention of Graves or Christophe. It was a little frusterating, but I still loved the book.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />I would also like to comment that someone mentioned a spin-off. I don't know if it's true or not, but I hope to God if there is a spin-off it's not about Graves as the main character and if it is....there better not be another love triangle or I'm going on strike! SERIOUSLY!!!!!!! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9009051463114780898">I'm going to start this rantview by stating that I love me some Lilith Saintcrow. I love her "Jill Kismet" series. I have hopes for her "Dante Valentine" series. I enjoyed her "Strange Angels" series & while the last three books made me want to smother Dru with my god-sister's Hello Kitty Tiger Pillow, I stuck it out like the book masochist/loyal fan I am. But this? This is WTFsauce with a side of "Bitch, Please!"<br/><br/>I cannot believe she did this. I can't. I'm in shock. Somebody bitch slap me out of</span>
  <span id="freeText9009051463114780898" style="display:none">I'm going to start this rantview by stating that I love me some Lilith Saintcrow. I love her "Jill Kismet" series. I have hopes for her "Dante Valentine" series. I enjoyed her "Strange Angels" series &amp; while the last three books made me want to smother Dru with my god-sister's Hello Kitty Tiger Pillow, I stuck it out like the book masochist/loyal fan I am. But this? This is WTFsauce with a side of "Bitch, Please!"<br><br>I cannot believe she did this. I can't. I'm in shock. Somebody bitch slap me out of this nightmare. If it wasn't bad enough what went down in "Reckoning", a friend links me to Saintcrow's post which pretty much says (to me) that us fans are a bunch of dumbasses for thinking that a part of this series revolves around the love triangle between Dru/Graves/Christophe.<br><br><i>Dru’s best friend, Graves, and her strange and handsome savior, Christophe, are ready to help her take on the ultimate evil. But will their battle for Dru’s heart get in the way of her survival?</i><br><br>That's in the blurb for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6600807.Jealousy__Strange_Angels___3_" title="Jealousy (Strange Angels, #3) by Lili St. Crow" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1268444217s/6600807.jpg" alt="Jealousy (Strange Angels, #3) by Lili St. Crow" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>. *blink blink* *blink blink* Well, of course. Only a completely sane person would read that &amp; not think "LOVE TRIANGLE!" Right? RIGHT?!? And all good love triangles must end. And here is where the inevitable spoilery comes in. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Apparently, in Saintcrow-land, all good love triangle's DON'T end. They go on &amp; on until the male halves die of blue balls. I understand that maybe there were a lot people on Team Christophe &amp; a lot on Team Graves &amp; maybe Saintcrow didn't know what to do. But FFS! Even Stephanie Meyer ended up choosing Edward for Belladumbass! She didn't end the series with B stringing Edward &amp; Jacob along no matter how many fans probably sent her death threats to make Jake the man for B! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>As others have said after reading this book, Cop Out. I debated on whether I should post this but it's been pissing me off since I finished this book &amp; I've been told that ranting is very therapeutic &amp; will aid in keeping you from ending up on Snapped. Or turning into that creepy dude in The Crow. So there you go. I still like Saintcrow <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I lie. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but right now, this series can kick rocks. I haven't been this damn heated since Eugenie took her brain damaged ass to Slutville in daisy dukes &amp; roller skates in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8840097.Iron_Crowned__Dark_Swan___3_" title="Iron Crowned (Dark Swan, #3) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Iron Crowned</a>.<br><br>ETA: When I copied &amp; pasted this rantreview from my word document, I accidentally left out a part. Even though it was written after the first spoiler tag, I'm going to put it here. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What pisses me off more than anything is not that Dru didn't choose the guy I wanted her to. I could give two craps who she chose. What I didn't like is that she chose NO ONE. A big part of this series is the budding romance between Dru, Christophe &amp; Graves &amp; Dru chose no one. Then Saintcrow says something a long the lines of "I don't think a woman should be defined by who she dates" &amp; I'm thinking to myself "Riiight. I'm not an author but if I was &amp; I was writing a female protagonist who isn't defined by who she dates, I sure as hells wouldn't throw a big ass love triangle into my damn series." But maybe that's just me. Maybe the best way to convey that a heroine doesn't need a guy is to make her cow-eyed &amp; weak at the knees over two guys. Yeah....WTFever, Saintcrow. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Now I'm done-in more ways than one.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_228600027" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228600027" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5496481-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576637295p2/5496481.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228600027?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/5496481-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5496481-becky?shelf=will-not-read-again">will-not-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5496481-becky?shelf=missing-parent-syndrome">missing-parent-syndrome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5496481-becky?shelf=dreaded-love-triangle">dreaded-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5496481-becky?shelf=special-snowflake-syndrome">special-snowflake-syndrome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228600027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1664277261087651709">I have mixed feelings about this book, and am going to (tentatively) give it a 2 star rating until my feelings about this book have solidified more.<br/><br/>The major strength of this series is the characters, and we do get to see everybody grow and change, which was a major plus. The sticking point for me is the ending.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Choosing to have Dru end up more or less alone at the end was an interesting stance to take, especially considering the rampant I'll-love-you-forever books overwhelming the</span></span>
  <span id="freeText1664277261087651709" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about this book, and am going to (tentatively) give it a 2 star rating until my feelings about this book have solidified more.<br /><br />The major strength of this series is the characters, and we do get to see everybody grow and change, which was a major plus. The sticking point for me is the ending.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Choosing to have Dru end up more or less alone at the end was an interesting stance to take, especially considering the rampant I'll-love-you-forever books overwhelming the YA genre right now. That being said, the ending also felt like a little bit of a cop-out. Graves opts to leave, promising to return later, citing his (fairly justifiable) personal issues. According to him, he needs to be "worth her" before he comes back. Christophe, meanwhile, remains behind and asks Dru if he has a chance. Dru is unsure, and Christophe says he's willing to wait.<br /><br />This, I think, was a problematic way to handle the love triangle--not because Dru chooses to be alone, but because Dru NEVER CHOOSES AT ALL. Graves makes the decision for her by leaving, and Dru is devastated. Meanwhile, Christophe is getting majorly shafted by her lack of commitment to him. I mean, I was rooting for Graves until the end, and even I thought Christophe was getting screwed. <br /><br />The other major problem in this situation for me was the massive Dru-worship that was going on at the end. I'm the first to admit that Dru is an awesome and hilarious character. But she's also flawed, and it bothered me that Graves felt he wasn't "worth her" at the end. In the prior books, their interactions had been fairly realistic: they both had their faults, and cared for each other despite (and because of!) them. And while it was sweet that Christophe was willing to wait for Dru, it was also kind of weirdly pathetic. Surely a super-hot, multi-lingual vampire can find a girl that's KIND OF interested in him? Heck, maybe that would kick Dru in gear.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Basically, I'm not sure that this book knew what it wanted to be--like the series as a whole, it jumps back and forth between funny and angsty, romantic and serious. While this can be handled well by some authors, as a reader, it felt like the author (or the publishing company) couldn't decide what kind of book (and series!) they wanted this to be. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1664277261087651709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8920585078740143068"><b>I literally cannot find an accurate reason to why I read the entire Strange Angels series. </b><br/><br/>The series was suggested to me by someone who said it was similar to Vampire Academy. I haven’t been in contact with that certain person in quite a while, but If I was, I would suggest the most dreadful and terrible series ever to be published, and be absolutely sure this particular person reads it. <br/><br/>Oh wait, I’m able to summon up a reason. It was the love triangle. I desperately needed to know who Dru ende</span>
  <span id="freeText8920585078740143068" style="display:none"><b>I literally cannot find an accurate reason to why I read the entire Strange Angels series. </b><br /><br />The series was suggested to me by someone who said it was similar to Vampire Academy. I haven’t been in contact with that certain person in quite a while, but If I was, I would suggest the most dreadful and terrible series ever to be published, and be absolutely sure this particular person reads it. <br /><br />Oh wait, I’m able to summon up a reason. It was the love triangle. I desperately needed to know who Dru ended up with, and I also wanted to know what the heroine’s name (Dru) was short for. <br /><br />So, I was basically expecting just two things from this book to be delivered. Of course, at the end she doesn’t end up with anyone and the author never tells us what Dru is short for. <br /><br /><b>The whole plot consisted of:</b><br /><br />Dru running<br />Dru getting caught but escapes<br /><br />Dru running <br />Dru getting caught but escapes <br /><br />Dru running<br />Dru getting caught – Dru not escaping until 30-40 pages later. (The final not so epic battle)<br /><br />And I’m not even exaggerating. It seriously happened three times in the book. She run and got caught three times. How the fuck did she even survive? The plot is predictable right from book one. We all know our little worthless (I don’t care if she’s physically strong, she's still worthless) heroine is going to defeat the big bad evil antagonist. <br /><br />After, completing the book I felt robbed of time. I realized that in the entire book there were only boring action scenes – no precise storyline besides fighting, punching and exploding dynamites. It was like watching a dull movie just for the cool visual effects. <br /><br /><b>Save yourself the time and don’t read the complete series.</b> <br /></span>

<div id="review_231735434" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231735434" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4353420-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321238012p2/4353420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231735434?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/4353420-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4353420-summer?shelf=series-with-bad-endings">series-with-bad-endings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer231735434&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231735434" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4888346170152657859">Let me first start out by saying, I loved every other on of the books. They kept me reading and wanting the next one as soon as possible... but this one? I loved up until it started nearing the end. The whole time I'm getting closer to the end I was thinking "how is this going to be tied up in such a small amount of pages left" and soon my question would be answered. It wouldn't be tied up! Not a single loose end! We don't know what happened to Graves, Dru, Christophe, their love triangle, nothi</span>
  <span id="freeText4888346170152657859" style="display:none">Let me first start out by saying, I loved every other on of the books. They kept me reading and wanting the next one as soon as possible... but this one? I loved up until it started nearing the end. The whole time I'm getting closer to the end I was thinking "how is this going to be tied up in such a small amount of pages left" and soon my question would be answered. It wouldn't be tied up! Not a single loose end! We don't know what happened to Graves, Dru, Christophe, their love triangle, nothing! And I personally hated that! I was soooo excited to read this just to be let down. <br /><br />In this post by Lilith SaintCrow, the author<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.lilithsaintcrow.com/forum/viewtopic.php?f=9&amp;t=1633&amp;start=30">http://www.lilithsaintcrow.com/forum/...</a><br /><br />She tells us this isn't about "which boy will she choose, its about her growing up" but then why did she make the love triangle such a big part of the book, just to leave us hanging! I think it's wonderful that the story is about her growing up, but she left so much out in the open. When I read a series, I get very into it. Like I am following people on their journey and I have to say when I finished Reckoning I just felt...heartbroken you could say? I felt like all of the sudden I wasn't allowed to follow them on their journey and was just left hanging and that is a terrible feeling.<br /><br />I guess in conclusion I can say, I loved it until the end. It would be a favorite series of mine if it just had an actually ending. I truly hope she writes more to the series but as of right now, I cannot recommend this to anyone. Too much left undone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4888346170152657859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_227984021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227984021" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227984021?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=nook">nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227984021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17832963980522231047">Loved it! The entire book was action packed and had me cheering for a great YA heroine! 4.5 to 5 star book...<i>easy</i>.<br/><b>Until the ending knocked it down to 3 stars.</b><br/>*<i>balloon deflates...</i>*<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[What the hell?! I thought this was the <i>last</i> book in a series? Doesn't that <i>usually</i> mean that loose ends <b>finally</b> get tied up?! Nothing gets resolved at the end of this one. NOTHING! <br/>Ok. That's not fair. Sergi finally bites it.<br/>But then it becomes apparent that it's <i>not really over</i>. The vampires <i>will</i> regroup</span></span>
  <span id="freeText17832963980522231047" style="display:none">Loved it! The entire book was action packed and had me cheering for a great YA heroine! 4.5 to 5 star book...<i>easy</i>.<br /><b>Until the ending knocked it down to 3 stars.</b><br />*<i>balloon deflates...</i>*<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What the hell?! I thought this was the <i>last</i> book in a series? Doesn't that <i>usually</i> mean that loose ends <b>finally</b> get tied up?! Nothing gets resolved at the end of this one. NOTHING! <br />Ok. That's not fair. Sergi finally bites it.<br />But then it becomes apparent that it's <i>not really over</i>. The vampires <i>will</i> regroup and it will all start again.<br />Well, that's not <i>so</i> bad, you say. I mean, we all imagine that the characters' lives will keep going even after the book ends, right?<br />Yes. <b>But</b> you like to imagine that your favorite characters are in a better position to handle things. You know, because they've been on this harrowing journey and come out on top.<br />So the main question is, did Dru grow into her role as basically the Top Dog of the Order? Meh. Not so much. Last I read, she kind of <i>sat in</i> on an important meeting and let the Big Boys do all the talking. Whew! <i>That's</i> impressive. <br />For a character who is so tough and resourceful while she's on the run, she's a real limp noodle when it comes to making a power play. Again, this is the <b>LAST</b> book. I expected her to grow a pair and lay down the law, not sit quietly and sniffle.<br />Whatever. I <i>could</i> have overlooked it if it hadn't been for this next thing.<br /><br /><b>HUGE ROMANTIC @#%ING COP-OUT!</b><br /><br />Annoyingly enough, this series has always had the dreaded (my opinion) Love Triangle. Most books seem to thrive on it, so who am I to argue? Personally, I've always loved Graves. Her best friend who slowly grew and changed into something <i>more</i> in her eyes. He started off gawky and unattractive, and grew into a cutie pie. Now, Christophe? Not so much. He was the unbelievably hot guy who started immediately sniffing around her...<i>even though he was so old he had <b>also</b> been in love with her <b>mother</b>!</i> Oh God! It burns! Ewwwww!<br />I held out hope, because Dru was <i>also</i> rightfully creeped out by the fact that he had wanted her mamma. <br />However, he <i>was</i> always there for her, and willing to sacrifice anything to keep her safe. Yes, he was icky, but by the end of this book I actually felt sorry for him. I think maybe <i>that</i> pisses me off more than anything else. The ending was so lame, that I was forced to feel sorry for the guy I <b>didn't like</b>!<br /><br />What happened, you ask? Was the ending <i>really</i> so bad? It's a Love Triangle, right? She picks one guy, and the other slinks home with his tail (or fangs) between his legs....<i>right</i>? Right?!<br />'Cause it's (again) the <b>Last Book</b>. I paid money to see how this was all going to turn out.<br /><br />I know what you're thinking. <br /><i>Spit it out, woman! Don't just keep us all sitting here in suspense!</i><br /><br />Ok, here it is.<br />She finally admits that to Graves that she loves him. He admits that he loves her, too. <b>But</b> he needs to get his head together so he can be 'worth her', and then he takes off with some of the of the other wulfen. He promises to come back to her. She cries and says she'll wait for him. Blah, blah, blah.<br /><br />You: <i>Well, that's not <b>so</b> bad.</i><br />Me: <i>Ah, but there's <b>more</b>.</i><br /><br />Christophe nearly killed himself trying to save her with a blood transfusion toward the end. Poor guy. But so what? He's creepy, and I didn't like him.<br /><i>Still</i>...<br />After Graves leaves, she goes to visit him in the infirmary, and basically tells him that she appreciates everything he has done for her, but it makes her feel weird that he's so much older than her, and was <b>IN LOVE WITH HER MOTHER</b>.<br /><br />You: <i>But that's what you <b>wanted</b> her to say, dumbass!</i><br />Me: <i>Ah, but there's <b>more</b>.</i><br /><br />She tells him she's not ready for a relationship with <i>anyone</i> right now. <br /><br />You: <i>Wait. didn't she just tell Graves she loved him? Was going to wait for him to come back to her? Oh well, you're probably just overreacting. The poor guy almost <b>died</b>. She's just trying to let him down easy. What a nice girl!</i><br />Me: <i>Ah, but there's <b>more</b>.</i><br /><br />Christophe asks if there's a <i>chance for him in the future</i>. And she says...<b>Yes.</b> It's in <i>that</i> moment that I feel sorry for the poor bastard. <br /><br />You: <i>*crickets chirping*</i><br />Me: Told ya.<br /><br />So in the end, nothing has changed. She still is not willing to become a real voice in the Order, both guys are still on the string, and the last scene of the book is Dru and Nat planning a shopping trip. What a load of crap. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I <i>did</i> sleep on this rating last night. If I had written this review yesterday, I probably would have rated it 2 stars. The vast majority of the book was good, though. Too bad about the lame-ass ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17832963980522231047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_159762675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159762675" />
    <a title="Kate (Nomalicious Reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2850603-kate-nomalicious-reads"><img alt="Kate (Nomalicious Reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397604375p2/2850603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159762675?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate (Nomalicious Reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate (Nomalicious Reads)" href="/user/show/2850603-kate-nomalicious-reads">Kate (Nomalicious Reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2850603-kate-nomalicious-reads?shelf=2011-releases">2011-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2850603-kate-nomalicious-reads?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2850603-kate-nomalicious-reads?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159762675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15857105737361867234"><b>More reviews can be found at my blog:</b> <a href='http://www.nomaliciousreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nomalicious Reads</a><br/><br/>Being a big fan of the Strange Angel's series I was beyond excited to get my hands on Reckoning, the final book in the series to find out what would happen to Dru and her companions... then the book came out and not being able to wait patiently for it to get to my mailbox I started reading reviews zealously and became terrified.<br/><br/>That's right, reviews... made me terrified to read the end of one of my favourite series!<br/><br/>After I read some people's</span>
  <span id="freeText15857105737361867234" style="display:none"><b>More reviews can be found at my blog:</b> <a href="http://www.nomaliciousreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Nomalicious Reads</a><br /><br />Being a big fan of the Strange Angel's series I was beyond excited to get my hands on Reckoning, the final book in the series to find out what would happen to Dru and her companions... then the book came out and not being able to wait patiently for it to get to my mailbox I started reading reviews zealously and became terrified.<br /><br />That's right, reviews... made me terrified to read the end of one of my favourite series!<br /><br />After I read some people's negative comments that the ending was 'shit' and other not so nice words I started to question and pick apart all the bad things that could happen at the end, that she could end up with the wrong guy, that everyone was going to DIE... so when Reckoning finally showed up in the mail I placed it wearily on the shelf next to the others in the series and backed away to a safe distance in case it exploded.<br /><br />Not really.. I'm just being melodramatic, cause I'm awesome like that!<br /><br />But no, I really did leave it on the shelf for too long, but putting my big girl pants on (an no not Bridget Jone's granny pants version) I finally picked up Reckoning, thinking 'Meh, what could be so bad?'<br /><br />...Nothing really. After all my melodrama I found myself quite enjoying it, even the "horrible" ending wasn't as bad as people made it out to be. Sure I can see why everyone was chucking a hissy, but I thought that it was a satisfying ending for the book and for what Dru had been through, the conclusion reflected the person she was at that exact moment.<br /><br />Was it a good ending for the end of a series? Hell no! It felt too much like an ending you would have knowing that there was another book coming, or a new series coming out shortly after... I would like to see more development more of a conclusion, a lot of the new problems that came out from the end of Reckoning deserve to be solved... So is Dru's story finished? I bloody well hope not! But hey who knows! (further investigation is needed on my part)<br /><br />I'm satisfied, yet unsatisfied and it's possible that I wasn't raging mad because I expected the apocalypse of all endings.<br /><br />So now that my little confession and rant is over I should probably talk about the rest of the book! Reckoning had what all the other Strange Angel books had...<br /><br />Those being:<br /><br /> * Dru being an idiot at times and me wanting to kill her.<br /> * Dru being her normal hilarious, kick-ass and snarky self.<br /> * Graves... being kick-ass, yet still hot and nerdy.<br /> * Christophe being douchey and hot at the same time.<br /> * Ash being adorable!<br /> * Running away from bad guy, being caught by bad guy, escaping again and kicking ass.<br /> * Oh and of course the standard... Dru not being able to decide on which boy awesome guy or creepy yet hot old dude to choose.<br /><br />Okay so you get the drift, I'm not mocking or anything, I actually like all these things... I must admit though I wanted more action, more romance and I found some things were just a repeat of all the other books rolled up to the bad guy actually dying this time. It was good yet I just wanted MORE!<br /><br />I really really really really hope that Lili St. Crow isn't finished telling Dru's story because although I didn't mind the ending, there is just so much left unsaid, new mysteries to solve and definitely a lot of room for her to grow into the awesome leader she should be. (not to mention other character's development after what happens!)<br /><br />Reckoning<br />By Lili St. Crow<br />Gets:<br />3 and a half nomalicious nomnom noms</span>
  <a data-text-id="15857105737361867234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11952956372955561995">*Rating* 2.5<br/>*Genre* YA Paranormal<br/><br/>*Review*<br/><br/>Five books. Five books and the only thing we definitely know is that the bad guy got dead. Yes, I did say got dead sue me! <br/><br/>Five books and Dru ends up with a penny, instead of a hundred dollar bill.   <span id="freeText11952956372955561995" style="display:none">*Rating* 2.5<br />*Genre* YA Paranormal<br /><br />*Review*<br /><br />Five books. Five books and the only thing we definitely know is that the bad guy got dead. Yes, I did say got dead sue me! <br /><br />Five books and Dru ends up with a penny, instead of a hundred dollar bill. Readers divided themselves into Team Christophe and Graves only to be left holding the bag with this release and the subsequent decisions by both Graves and Dru. So, again, what was the point in continuing this series past the first three books?<br /><br />Then there is the puzzling realization that Dru's family still has more secrets that they never told her. Secrets that nobody will end up learning the facts behind because this is the last book of the series!<br /><br />So, again I ask, what was the point? I'm feeling totally cheated right now, and it's not even this series ending that I've had a problem with. It's been all THREE that I've read!<br /><br />Was the point to show how much Dru changes after her "blooming" only to have her cry for nearly 125 pages? Yeah, we kind of got that by the way she continually described her "enhanced" features time and time again.<br /><br />I'll say it. I hate Graves. I think Christophe actually seemed more interested in keeping her safe and away from harm and was there at the when Dru needed him the most. Naturally, I still think he is also the George Soros creepy dude of this series who went after Dru's mother and now wants a little nookie with Dru as well!<br /><br />I can't in good faith recommend this book to anyone. I know this will come as a puzzling proposition to anyone who actually reads my reviews and comments on them.<br /><br />Thanks by the way to those who do.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer544765056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9266970120196557150">Man oh man, what a conclusion. Lili St. Crow writes emotions and mixed feelings so damned well. I could feel the frustration and self-hate and confusion that Dru experiences like they were my own emotion.<br/><br/>Dru is on the run with Ash and Graves, not returning to the Order, since they sold her out once and she is unwilling to trust herself to them again, since they're not the most reliable at keeping her afe. Dru figures she's just as safe (or not) on her own. The trio runs away, gets into trouble (</span>
  <span id="freeText9266970120196557150" style="display:none">Man oh man, what a conclusion. Lili St. Crow writes emotions and mixed feelings so damned well. I could feel the frustration and self-hate and confusion that Dru experiences like they were my own emotion.<br /><br />Dru is on the run with Ash and Graves, not returning to the Order, since they sold her out once and she is unwilling to trust herself to them again, since they're not the most reliable at keeping her afe. Dru figures she's just as safe (or not) on her own. The trio runs away, gets into trouble (inevitably), and there's nonstop action throughout the book. There's not a dull moment in the book. In this book, of all things, a new supernatural sect, the djinn, are introduced, and goody goody gumdrops, they're out to get Dru too. Poor girl, she just bloomed, and now this. It seems like everything she touches explodes.<br /><br />Another thing that's well done in this series is the love triangle. Ok, it's unresolved, but there's so much believable internal conflict for Dru regarding the two potential love interest. It's not like other series where it's pretty damn obvious who's going to get the girl despite the supposed triangle, she really leaves us guessing...and guessing, since it's not really tied up. I'm rooting for the guy I like though, cause honestly, the other one is a huge jackass and has been for the whole series despite the whole saving Dru thing. It's pretty obvious to whom I'm referring, heh. I'm upset that the series isn't tied down cleanly and just ends RIGHT HERE but this has been the best YA paranormal I've read since the Vampire Academy series. And any comparison to Richelle Mead is not to be disregarded.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_231497549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231497549" />
    <a title="Dina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2333579-dina"><img alt="Dina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252548316p2/2333579.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231497549?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dina" href="/user/show/2333579-dina">Dina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231497549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10302659959957856667">Was I disappointed, I'm not sure. The book had endless adventures. There were some really interesting things we learned about Dru. Lots of questions still that were not answered. New questions added, such as the hexes she saw, the blue and red. I think the love triangle ended fine, but I still think she is a bit hard on Chris. She was honest with Graves but she wasn't honest with Chris completely, only telling him the things holding her back and never telling him the things that she adored about</span>
  <span id="freeText10302659959957856667" style="display:none">Was I disappointed, I'm not sure. The book had endless adventures. There were some really interesting things we learned about Dru. Lots of questions still that were not answered. New questions added, such as the hexes she saw, the blue and red. I think the love triangle ended fine, but I still think she is a bit hard on Chris. She was honest with Graves but she wasn't honest with Chris completely, only telling him the things holding her back and never telling him the things that she adored about him. It was a good move for the love triangle, although it was a dishonest move on Dru's part never letting Graves know that she had feelings for someone else too. Maybe because of his mental state, who knows, but I think both men are fragile in their own way. We don't get to understand the Anna presence in her head thing, and what happens to a person when they drink blood from another. <br /><br />I was torn from three stars or four. I really feel that for a series it needs more books. If we don't get more of Dru that's fine but others from other aspects of this world because we don't really get to understand "the world". <br /><br />I noticed that other readers talked about the repeating, and I get that too but the repeating I hate is stuff we know about already, lets get some explanations for things that are new, not old. <br /><br />For example, the Hiro nodding thing, I don't really care if she nods back every time, at first it was interesting, but we don't get any more information on Hiro, other then it appears he respects Dru but seems to dislike Chris quite a bit. <br /><br />The other part of her that we don't understand is the Faulk family touch and what other skills she has. We don't get find any of that out because we are introduced to it as a specialty at the end of the book. Oddly Chris must have known there was something special about her, he had to have because of the odd ways she had defended herself, such as the bathroom attack, but he never talked to her about it. Also, why was she loosing some of her abilities, such as when she was drugged, why couldn't she detect it?<br /><br />It's hard for me to feel as if this book really did act as the final, maybe a final for the death of the vampire king, but not really for this story about Dru and all the oddities that it contained. I hope there is more, and if not, I hope for the other books series she writes, she doesn't leave so much out of the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10302659959957856667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_215823106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/215823106" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6461002-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317095390p2/6461002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/215823106?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/6461002-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer215823106&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer215823106" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5010907456115028083">I would have finished the book in one sitting if not for school and assignments and my Lit in English portfolio. Anyhow, i finished the book in 3 days, which is as good as i could get under such circumstances.<br/><br/>Ooo-kay. Final book. I really can't do the no spoilers thing. Everything i am gonna write is spoilery. Sorry, guys.<br/><br/>Dru has bloomed, as anyone who has read Defiance would know. And i am very, very glad for that. She gets to seriously kick some ass and fight. Oh yay, I love to see my Dru-girl</span>
  <span id="freeText5010907456115028083" style="display:none">I would have finished the book in one sitting if not for school and assignments and my Lit in English portfolio. Anyhow, i finished the book in 3 days, which is as good as i could get under such circumstances.<br /><br />Ooo-kay. Final book. I really can't do the no spoilers thing. Everything i am gonna write is spoilery. Sorry, guys.<br /><br />Dru has bloomed, as anyone who has read Defiance would know. And i am very, very glad for that. She gets to seriously kick some ass and fight. Oh yay, I love to see my Dru-girl fight. Bascially the whole book centres around escaping and on the run from Sergej--fighting and on the run again--and escaping again. There. I spoiled it.<br /><br />My Dru-girl. As smart as she is with following her grandmother's owl (i.e. her aspect in animal form and her instinct), she is really lost and confused when it comes to her relationships with Graves and Christophe. Mind you, i am Team Christophe, ALL THE WAY. The confusion in Dru, for the first time, annoys me. As much i love it, i can't believe she is so dumb when it comes to love. Or, is it that girls are always dumb when it comes down to this, and it's just that they can't cope with the idea of them not being able to handle it, and so they say they hate it?<br /><br />Dru did a lot of growing up in this book. She actually saves people, instead of being the one who is constantly saved by others, which i am glad to say i am very happy and proud about this. Dru is sixteen only. The things she faced--mum hiding her and getting killed, grandmother dying, dad turning into zombie and having to kill him--is not what a normal person can't comprehend with. It leaves a scar in that person's heart, which is exactly what the author's trying to say in the book. No matter how deep down you try to hide that box of feelings or how hard you try to make yourself forget that, they stay. And the only thing we can do is cope with the fact that they stay, until your heart stops beating. <br /><br />One of the reason why i like Dru so much and that she is my ever-fave protagonist is that she stays strong even when she's scared. She is not afraid of taking others up as her responsibility, even if it means being caught or exposed or endangered. She just does that. And at certain points i think she is too tough on herself that she seems to take all the blame and burden when they are not hers to bear. She un-Broke Ash, my fave wulfen. And so Ash's loyalty stays. That's how she wins people over--by being true and genuine in helping or in this case, fihgting for others. Being a full-bloomed svetocha means she has grown into all of her abilities, apart from the skills she has yet to learn from Christophe. She is strong, literally. But is she strong enough to stand against Sergej? Yes, she is, with a slight hand from Christophe. Another reason why i like Dru so much is her voice. Yes, the voice that narrates the whole story. I like her cynicism and her sacarsm. I especially like the fact that she swears. She sounds real, with that. I like that she still manages to see things with optimism and stay determined at the worst of times, especailly during the Dibs and blood confusion scene (now, i am trying to keep it as spoilers-free as possible. i did put some effort). I like the way she does whatever she has to to save others and herself, even if it means lying and possible getting herself killed.<br /><br />Christophe. I am completely haert-broken as to how ashen he looks at certain scenes. The way he thinks he can never save or do enough for Dru really makes my heart ache, though i didn't cry in the whole book. He is scray, granted. But is he not good enough for Dru? In my opinion, not at all. Just because he's done something bad in the past, or maybe things that are only bad when we see it now, doesn't take away the fact he is a good person, in nature. Just because he hides it doesn't take away the fact also. I hate to see him weak at the last scene, afraid of what Dru may say. Okay. Maybe i have taken for granted that he has to be strong all the time. I know it's not fair. But that's what i like about him. No matter how bad and terrible and utterly hopeless the situation is, he fights, till the end, for Dru. The blood confusion scene in the helicopter (i assume it takes place in the helicopter) nearly kills me, again. As much as Dru kind of breaks his heart, at least he does not lose to Graves (or did he actually?). Well, at least he earns an I don't know from Dru instead of a No, which, i guess, is the best he, and i could ask for. I am absolutely sure he's gonna stay in my heart as my most beloved hero and male character for a very, very long period of time.<br /><br />Graves. Not that i don't like him. I just don't like the fact that he treats Dru with whatever comes to his mind. I know he loves her. And i know love makes people do crazy things, but making Dru as confused as that and get all jealous on her? Umm, NO. That's not a way to treat the girl you love.I don't care how fucked-up his post-Dru life has been. He hurts her, even more than he imagines because he means a lot to Dru. I swear, no matter how mad Christophe is at Dru, he will NOT do that to her. Yup. That's right. I am Team Christophe. Granted, what Graves does for Dru at the near end of the book proves he can do as well as Christophe in protecting and saving Dru. I am not denying that. It's simply a matter of preference, and types.<br /><br />The book/series has kind of an open ending. Nothing's solid. Sergej's dead but nosferats are just confused. Graves leaving and Dru rejecting Christophe. And Dru's grandmother being related to those hex people. Crazy as ever politics that Dru has to deal with, together with the Order. The Real World is just as it was before. Basically nothing has been acheived. Maybe it seems that i am dismissing whatever Dru has done through in the five books, but that's how life is. Just because you put in your hardest doesn't mean you are immune to hardships and trying times and you are invinsible. Life goes on as it was before. The state of the ending exactly reflects and portrays how life, in reality, is, and i really appreciate it. It's true that me being Team Christophe does not get the ending i want. But Dru is only sixteen. Who knows how she'll think when she matures even more? And that's life. People stay and people go, and the world still continues to revolve. The ending is very, very meaningful and i don't think many YA fictions can do that. Once again, this book proves that lilith St. Crow, as an author, does wonder. With such an ending, i am immensely satisfied. Maybe even a bit more satisfied than the ending that i imagined in my post-reading-Reckoning period where Dru ends up with Chris, because we all know that both Graves and Chris mean a lot to Dru. And that's how life is. The ending of Reckoning is practically the closest-to-reality and perfect ending i have ever gotten in an YA series/book.<br /><br />Thanks for ending, guys. I know it's super, uber long. Not exactly what i would have written for any book noramlly. But hey, this is the final book, and Ms St. Crow deserves this.<br /><br />Until next time. X</span>
  <a data-text-id="5010907456115028083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_177310974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177310974" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4162498-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350161204p2/4162498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177310974?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/4162498-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177310974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14405672054820522961">Okay, the jacket doesn't look like something I'd picture on Dru, but I love this cover! The model is perfect (and yea for having the same girl on all the covers), exactly what I'd picture Dru would look like, and I love the aspect running through her.<br/><br/>I can't wait to read this book, but it sucks that it's the last one in the series.<br/><br/>************<br/><br/>7/22/12 - In <i>Reckoning</i>, Dru, Graves and Ash are on the run following their escape from Sergej. Dru has decided to go to the last, safest place she has, eve</span>
  <span id="freeText14405672054820522961" style="display:none">Okay, the jacket doesn't look like something I'd picture on Dru, but I love this cover! The model is perfect (and yea for having the same girl on all the covers), exactly what I'd picture Dru would look like, and I love the aspect running through her.<br /><br />I can't wait to read this book, but it sucks that it's the last one in the series.<br /><br />************<br /><br />7/22/12 - In <i>Reckoning</i>, Dru, Graves and Ash are on the run following their escape from Sergej. Dru has decided to go to the last, safest place she has, even though she knows they won’t be able to stay there forever. She heads to her grandmother’s, now her, house in the South. Once there things actually end up going from bad to worse and the three eventually find themselves on the run again. I really don’t want to give anything else away. A lot of the characters from the previous books eventually pop up and I liked their roles in the book, though I do wish that some of them had had a little more face time, even though I know that the nature of the book, being on the run, etc. didn’t really allow for it. We know there’s going to be a showdown with Sergej, which I thought would be The Dru Show, but it went down a little differently and I really liked it. There were a couple of little twists in the book, which didn’t shock me and I liked the way they eventually came about, as well as more revelations about Dru’s past and her family. I wasn’t expecting some of them and they kind of came out of nowhere, but, again, I liked them. St. Crow also introduces a new type of character into the series, which ends up causing some of the bigger moments in the book.<br /><br />As with the rest of the books in the series, St. Crow is really descriptive. All the time. <i>Great gulping heaves, tearing through me like a crowd of hobnailed boots against a street, beating out cadence.</i> Overall, I like it, but, for some reason it got on my nerves every once in a while in this one. I don’t know if she did it more, or what, but it did. Having said that, I really like St. Crow’s writing style. Her characters have a lot of depth and I like how she’s not afraid to have them get smacked around, they feel like crap after they’re in a fight or Dru feels like she has to do something like pee when she’s running from the latest threat and has the snot scared out of her. A lot of times characters will be on the run for days and you never hear about them being hungry, dirty, smelly, scared crapless or tired. Despite their supernatural abilities, St. Crow gives most of her characters all of these normal feelings and needs. It’s one of the qualities I’ve always liked about the books, because, despite the abnormal situations, it makes the characters seem realistic.<br /><br />Even though I really liked most of this book, I <i>hated</i> one part, a big part, of it: the end. Since it’s very spoilery, I’ve hidden it. Though I can cuss like a sailor in person, I tend to not do it in my reviews, so, just a warning, in the spoiler the gloves are off. That’s how pissed I am about one part of the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What the supermotherfucking FUCK?! Okay, I can understand how Dru might not be able to choose between Christophe or Graves right after everything that happened. I also get why Graves would need to leave for a while. Yeah, he’s an idiot for thinking he’s not worthy of Dru, but I see why he’d feel that way. Sergej broke him and he betrayed Dru, even though he fought it and it was unintentional. And the way she treated Christophe?! I thought his attitude towards the wulfen needed a major adjustment (and he did seem to be less jerky to them in this book), but he <i>always</i> helped, protected and went after Dru whenever she needed him. Even after she told him she hated him and believed that he had turned Graves over to his father. He tried to rescue her, got caught and tortured and then volunteered to, and almost did, die to save her. What does she do? Go in and tell him he was creepy and too old for her. She didn’t even freaking thank him!!! Yes, I also thought it was a little icky that he seemed to dig her mom, though he did explain to Dru how differently he felt about her in a previous book. Also, he always spoke his mind, but he didn’t even try to persuade her or explain himself about anything she said, just asked if he had a chance with her. Really? I call bullshit. That was totally out of character for him. When I turned the page after that crapfest with Graves and Christophe (who, after lots of waffling, I wanted her to get together with) I saw an epilogue and thought, okay, St. Crow isn’t going to end a great series so ridiculously. She’s going to take us weeks, months, maybe even a year into the future and see what happened. Wrong!!! It got even worse. Chit chat about maybe shopping with Nat. That’s what the fucking epilogue is about? I don’t think epilogue means what St. Crow thinks it means. I was thrilled that, of the few reviews I read when I finished the book, the words that immediately popped into my head made it to other peoples’ reviews: cop out. What a cop out. I was so disappointed. I know it’s just a book and I kept, no keep, telling myself not to get so pissed about it, but I can feel my blood pressure rising even as I type this. It was like the author couldn’t make a decision or maybe had another deadline and figured to hell with this one, the series is over anyway. I don’t even care if she mulled it over for years and thought it was some super clever, girl power ending. Seriously one of the most disappointing finishes to, not just a book, but a series, in my opinion. The Strange Angels series is one of my favorites, it was so original and addictive, and the abrupt, not-an-ending ending just really took away from all of that for me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. If you don’t want to read the spoiler (which I wouldn’t recommend if you haven’t read the book), suffice it to say that, without the ending, or with a different one, <i>Reckoning</i> would’ve been close to five stars for me, but I had to knock a star off for the ending (I actually think I was being kind by having it be just one) and if I could rate the conclusion apart from the rest of the book, I’d give it no stars. I still love this series and would recommend it to anyone. Dru is one of my favorite heroines ever and Graves, Christophe, the wulfen and Nat are some of the best secondary characters around. However, the last few pages were a huge letdown and left me really disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14405672054820522961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2194714930919448615">Oh my Cheez-Its. That can't be the ending. SO MUCH IS LEFT IN A CLIFFHANGERRR.<br/><br/>*le sigh* I don't want to say much, in fear of spoiling anything. But I will say that this is a somewhat satisfying ending to this series. I do believe I felt more sorry for Graves than anybody. Then Christophe. Hell, I felt sorry for Dru. But then it's like, <i>Well you're kick-ass and stubborn. You'll find a way out of it eventually.</i> And man, there was a lot of action in this one too. I mean, dur. You're going to expect</span>
  <span id="freeText2194714930919448615" style="display:none">Oh my Cheez-Its. That can't be the ending. SO MUCH IS LEFT IN A CLIFFHANGERRR.<br /><br />*le sigh* I don't want to say much, in fear of spoiling anything. But I will say that this is a somewhat satisfying ending to this series. I do believe I felt more sorry for Graves than anybody. Then Christophe. Hell, I felt sorry for Dru. But then it's like, <i>Well you're kick-ass and stubborn. You'll find a way out of it eventually.</i> And man, there was a lot of action in this one too. I mean, dur. You're going to expect a shit-ton of action in a Lilith Saintcrow book.<br /><br />I feel like Graves wasn't in this book that much. I mean, I know it's nothing compared to <i>Defiance</i>. But still, this was the final book, and I feel like Christophe somewhat got all the heat. <i>
  <s>Even though I love him more than Graves.</s>
</i> I still like Graves though. c:<br /><br />There could definitely be a sixth book. And I'm not saying that like, "oh I heard somewhere that the author is writing another book." Noooo. I'm saying that like "there's a lot that's undone" type of way. Lili is notorious for endings like that, it seems. Her books leave you wondering. Big time. I read her <i>Dante Valentine</i> series that came out in one book... And it was <i>weird</i>. But a good type of weird. And it had an ending that was like..."WTF HAPPENS NOW?!" That's how I feel about the <i>Strange Angels</i> series. Like a few questions for instance. (Spoilery!!!!) Is Graves <i>really</i> coming back? Where does this leave Dru and Graves? Where does this leave Dru and <i>Christophe</i>? What's Dru's full name?<br /><br />UGH. I wish there was a sixth one. :( But this was an awesome finale~</span>

  <span id="freeText15168043009638188977" style="display:none">I'm still not 100% about what I think of the ending.<br />I did think it was realistic that Dru didn't choose 'the one' because she's still only a teenager but the triangle was a huge part of the series and it's just left unresolved so I feel a bit cheated.. unless of course their some spin off books which let us know Dru's future.. but i'm not holding my breath.... <br /><br />....I've come up with my own ending.. where dru dates a few different guys-has a few flings, a couple of passionate affairs, a steady relationship or two, has her heart broken, breaks other guys hearts.. and then she meets the one - Gristophe - Yes Graves and Christoph are now magically 1 person.. everyone's happy! <br /></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1764162045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13544848564641487757">Whaat? That's an ending?!? It's like the last part of this book is missing! I need some closure! Very unsatisfying open ending is all I have to say.<br/><br/>I am so annoyed with Dru and her actions right now, mad about the way the love-triangle was resolved (or should I say unresolved?) and just overall disappointed with this conclusion.<br/><br/>Not sure yet with the rating. I read it whole in a few days and it wasn't all bad, but I still may change it to 1 star just for the bullshit ending. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9bnzbfB6oVMU+A7VCZMyxpKS8WBu08/5Rmu8dYYc58OHNXZ+8fYlVn8M4NdQRSJiYGOmxQj+ILOxYhyKEKxOTw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nH0u6/VjnoQ28zHMfwMlbsw0SK03pTqlrU/U0rH9/UTu8av49O8agV0H384m1TXKPsUfCFGI1e9aRnQtJ01UyA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14147837076727919747">Lili St. Crow was born in New Mexico, bounced around the world as an Air Force brat, and fell in love with writing when she was ten years old. She lives in Vancouver, Washington, in a house full of stray cats and children.<br/><br/>Lili St. Crow also writes as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/131208.Lilith_Saintcrow' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lilith Saintcrow</a>.</span>

Her mentor Christophe is missing, her almost-boyfriend is acting weird, and the bodyguards she’s been assigned seem to know much more than they should.         script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>

      </div>

    </div>
